Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





This vulnerability allows an attacker website to include some javascript code that causes the victim browser to crash with all its tabs when he visits the malicious site. In particular the attacker javascript code has to execute three main operations in a loop to perform the attack successfully: join at least two interest groups with the same owner plus some specific fields, and then run an auction including the owner as interest group buyer.



<span class="line"><!---->This vulnerability allows an attacker website to include some javascript code that causes the victim browser to crash with all its tabs when he visits the malicious site. In particular the attacker javascript code has to execute three main operations in a loop to perform the attack successfully: join at least two interest groups with the same owner plus some specific fields, and then run an auction including the owner as interest group buyer.<!----></span>



<br>





The while loop is introduced because it is not guaranteed that every auction will generate a crash (from experimental results), but after some the probability increases and almost always works.



<span class="line"><!---->The while loop is introduced because it is not guaranteed that every auction will generate a crash (from experimental results), but after some the probability increases and almost always works.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>





:



<span class="line"><!---->:<!----></span>



<br>





Chrome Version: 114.0.5735.90 (Official Build) (64-bit) (cohort: M114_stable_rampup) 



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 114.0.5735.90 (Official Build) (64-bit) (cohort: M114_stable_rampup) <!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: all (mainly tested on Windows 10 Version 22H2 (Build 19045.2965))



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: all (mainly tested on Windows 10 Version 22H2 (Build 19045.2965))<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





To reproduce the issue, as listed below, the attacker javascript code has to execute three main operations in a loop to perform the attack successfully: join at least two interest groups with the same owner plus some specific fields, and then run an auction including the owner as interest group buyer.



<span class="line"><!---->To reproduce the issue, as listed below, the attacker javascript code has to execute three main operations in a loop to perform the attack successfully: join at least two interest groups with the same owner plus some specific fields, and then run an auction including the owner as interest group buyer.<!----></span>



<br>





The first interest group should contain at least a minimal number of fields: (owner, name, biddingLogicUrl, ads) and make sure that owner and biddingLogicUrl share the same https origin, and biddingLogicUrl contains a valid server resource (not necessarily a javascript file). An example of such an interest group is :



<span class="line"><!---->The first interest group should contain at least a minimal number of fields: (owner, name, biddingLogicUrl, ads) and make sure that owner and biddingLogicUrl share the same https origin, and biddingLogicUrl contains a valid server resource (not necessarily a javascript file). An example of such an interest group is :<!----></span>

<br>



<br>





The browser will crash because of a bug, not because of the while loop.



<span class="line"><!---->The browser will crash because of a bug, not because of the while loop.<!----></span>



<br>





The while loop is introduced because it is not guaranteed that every auction will generate a crash (from experimental results), but after some the probability increases.



<span class="line"><!---->The while loop is introduced because it is not guaranteed that every auction will generate a crash (from experimental results), but after some the probability increases.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





FOR CRASHES:



<span class="line"><!---->FOR CRASHES:<!----></span>



<br>





Type of crash: browser (all tabs of all profiles)



<span class="line"><!---->Type of crash: browser (all tabs of all profiles)<!----></span>



<br>





Crash state: not available



<span class="line"><!---->Crash state: not available<!----></span>



<br>





Client ID: 1914906351494781154



<span class="line"><!---->Client ID: 1914906351494781154<!----></span>

Sorry for my mistake on the issue labeling, I thought that it could be considered a security bug. I don't have much evidence, however we wanted to send the report because, maybe, it could be possible to further explore the vulnerability and use it to create a more serious attack. Our guess is that a security exception is thrown by the browser code when certain conditions are met even if we don’t know why exactly.

I wasn't able to repro this bug, at least on Linux -- see attached patch at my attempt to turn the repro instructions into an automated test.



<span class="line"><!---->I wasn't able to repro this bug, at least on Linux -- see attached patch at my attempt to turn the repro instructions into an automated test.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Note that I had to make some changes to the repro code to make it valid JS (for example, ig1 vs ig_1, adding missing commas, pointing at valid URLs, etc.)



<span class="line"><!---->Note that I had to make some changes to the repro code to make it valid JS (for example, ig1 vs ig_1, adding missing commas, pointing at valid URLs, etc.)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The code just runs for a long time without crashing (and then the test times out since no crash occurred, and the code would run forever without a timeout).



<span class="line"><!---->The code just runs for a long time without crashing (and then the test times out since no crash occurred, and the code would run forever without a timeout).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Is there some way to share working repro code / a repro site? Not sure if there's an easy way to do so in a non-public way, but if this isn't a security bug, it could only be used for denial of service, IIUC?

The issue seems to be on this line: [0]



<span class="line"><!---->The issue seems to be on this line: [0]<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





        bid_states_.pop_back();



<span class="line"><!---->        bid_states_.pop_back();<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The problem is we pop from the bid_states_, but we don't update the size_limit_ to match like we did in [1].



<span class="line"><!---->The problem is we pop from the bid_states_, but we don't update the size_limit_ to match like we did in [1].<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I can see that at after the pop, bid_states_.size() is 1, but size_limit_ is 2. This remains the case until the point of the crash, causing the index out of bounds.



<span class="line"><!---->I can see that at after the pop, bid_states_.size() is 1, but size_limit_ is 2. This remains the case until the point of the crash, causing the index out of bounds.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





My repro page (which normally crashes in a few seconds on a dev build) didn't crash in over a minute after adding this line after the `bid_states_.pop_back();`:



<span class="line"><!---->My repro page (which normally crashes in a few seconds on a dev build) didn't crash in over a minute after adding this line after the `bid_states_.pop_back();`:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





        size_limit_ = std::min(size_limit_, bid_states_.size());



<span class="line"><!---->        size_limit_ = std::min(size_limit_, bid_states_.size());<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So we have a fix -- once I find a way to test this change, we can submit. Thanks to 



<span class="line"><!---->So we have a fix -- once I find a way to test this change, we can submit. Thanks to <!----></span>





behamilton@google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/behamilton@google.com"><!---->behamilton@google.com<!----></a>





 for helping look into this.

Fixes a browser process crash -- we are not seeing this crash in the wild, but the crash may be easily triggered by misbehaving scripts. Given that we intend to significantly ramp up the Protected Audiences (FLEDGE) API usage in M115, we'd like to merge back this crash fix. We *don't* believe this is a security issue, just stability.
